فههنا يريد نفي الحركة في الكم والكيف مع التنبيه على منشأ توهمهما، وذلك أنا نجد الجسم ينتقل على سبيل التدريج من كمية إلى كمية أخرى أزيد أو أنقص ومن كيفية إلى كيفية أخرى تضاد الأولى أو تماثلها من غير أن يظهر لنا تفاصيل ذلك وأزمنة وجود كل منها فنتوهم أن ذلك حركة إذ لا تعقل من الحركة إلا تغيراً على التدريج لكن لا حركة عند التحقيق لأن معنى التدريج المعتبر في الحركة أن لا يكون دفعة لا بحسب الذات، ولا بحسب الأجزاء والانتقال ههنا إنما هو دفعات يتوهم من اجتماعها التدريج لأن ما بين المبدأ والمنتهى من مراتب الكميات أو الكيفيات متمايزة بالفعل، ينتقل الجسم من كل منها إلى آخر دفعة كما في صيرورة الأرض ماء ثم هواء ثم ناراً مع الاتفاق ذلك ليس حركة جوهرية من الأرض إلى النار لظهور تفاصيل على أن مجموع المراتب وأزمنة وجوداتها ويدل على نفي الحركة في الأمور المتمايزة بالفعل سواء كانت كميات أو كيفيات أو جواهر أن الوسط بين المبدأ والمنتهى إن كان واحداً فظاهر أنه لا حركة، وإن كان كثيراً فتلك الكثرة سواء كان اختلافها بالنوع أو بالعدد أما أن تكون غير متناهية وهو محال ضرورة كونها محصورة بين حاصرين، وإما أن تكون متناهية وهو يستلزم تركب الحركة من أمور لا تقبل القسمة إذ لو انقسمت إلى أمور متغايرة ننقل الكلام إلى كل واحد منها، وهلم جرا، فيكون ما فرض متناهياً غير متناه هذا خلف وتركب الحركة مما لا يقبل الانقسام باطل لاستلزامه وجود الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ، وكون البطء لتخلل السكنات. أما الأول فلانطباق الحركة على ما فيه الحركة . أما الثاني فلأن السريع إذا تحرك جزءاً فالبطيء إن تحرك مثله دائماً لزم تساويهما أو أكثر لزم كونه أسرع أو أقل لزم انقسام ما لا ينقسم، فلم يبق إلا أن يكون له فيما بين أجزاء الحركة سكنات . وسيجيء بيان بطلان اللازمين وهذا بخلاف الحركة الأينية، فإن الوسط الذي بين المبدأ والمنتهى. أعني امتداد المسافة واحد بالفعل، يقبل بحسب الفرض انقسامات غير متناهية .

فإن قيل : يجوز أن يكون كل واحد من تلك الآحاد المتناهية قابلاً لانقسامات غير متناهية، فلا يلزم تركب الحركة مما لا تقبل الانقسام .

قلنا : هذا غير مقيد إذ التقدير أن الانتقال إلى كل من تلك الأحاد دفعى والحاصل أن امتناع تركب الحركة مما لا ينقسم يقتضي أن يكون امتدادها منطبقاً على أمر قابل لانقسامات غير متناهية على ما هو شأن لكم واحد كما في الحركة في الماء، أو الأجسام مختلفة كما في الحركة من الأرض إلى السماء لا على كم منفصل متناهي الآحاد سواء كان معروضه جوهراً، أو كماً متصلاً أو كيف أو غير ذلك، وبهذا يندفع ما يتوهم من أنه إذا جازت الحركة في المسافة لكونها معروضة لما يقبل الانقسام لا إلى نهاية، ففي الكم القابل لذلك بحسب ذاته أولى .
Here he intends to negate motion in quantity and quality while drawing attention to the source of their illusion. That is because we find the body gradually transitioning from one quantity to another greater or lesser, and from one quality to another contrary or similar, without the details and times of each appearing to us, so we imagine that this is motion, since motion is only conceived as gradual change. But in truth there is no motion, because the meaning of gradualness considered in motion is that it is not instantaneous neither in essence nor in parts, and the transition here is only instants of which gradualness is imagined, because the intermediate ranks of quantities or qualities between the beginning and end are actually distinct; the body transitions from each to the next instantaneously, as in the transformation of earth into water, then air, then fire—although this is not a substantial motion from earth to fire due to the appearance of details, but the totality of ranks and times of their existence [indicates...]. And it indicates the negation of motion in things that are actually distinct, whether quantities, qualities, or substances, that the middle between the beginning and end, if it is one, obviously there is no motion; if it is many, that multiplicity—whether its difference is by species or number—must either be infinite, which is impossible because it is bounded between two bounds, or finite, which entails composition of motion from indivisible parts, because if it were divided into different things, we would repeat the argument for each one, and so on, so what was assumed finite becomes infinite—this is a contradiction. And composition of motion from what does not admit division is false because it entails the existence of the indivisible part, and that slowness is due to the interpolation of rests. As for the first, [it is false] because of the application of motion to that in which motion occurs. As for the second, because if the quick moves a part, then if the slow always moves the like, they would be equal; if more, it would be faster; if less, it would entail division of what does not divide. So it remains only that it has rests between the parts of motion. And the proof of the falsity of both implications will come. This is unlike motion in place, for the middle between the beginning and end—i.e., the extension of distance—is one in actuality, admitting by assumption infinite divisions.

If it is said: It is possible that each of those finite units is divisible into infinite divisions, so the composition of motion from what does not admit division does not follow.

We reply: This is not valid, for the estimation is that the transition to each of those units is instantaneous. And the gist is that the impossibility of composition of motion from what does not divide requires that its extension corresponds to something susceptible to infinite divisions, as is the case for each one, like motion in water, or the bodies are different as in motion from earth to sky, not upon a discrete quantity with finite units, whether its substrate is substance, or continuous quantity, or quality, or other. And by this is refuted what is imagined, that if motion is permissible in distance because it is a substrate for what admits infinite division, then in quantity that admits that by itself, it is even more appropriate.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) refuting the notion of motion in the categories of quantity (al-kamm) and quality (al-kayf). The author begins by explaining the source of the illusion: we observe gradual transition in quantity and quality and mistakenly think it is motion, but true motion requires gradualness without instantaneousness. The transition here is actually a sequence of instantaneous changes (daf'at). The proof then argues that the intermediate stages between the beginning and end are actually distinct (mutamayyiza bi'l-fi'l). If the middle is one, there is no motion. If it is many, the multiplicity must be either infinite or finite. Infinite is impossible because it is bounded between two bounds. Finite entails motion composed of indivisible parts (ma la yaqbal al-qisma), because if we divide it, we repeat the argument, leading to an infinite regress. This composition is false because it implies the existence of the indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajzza) and that slowness is caused by rests (sakanat) between movements. He then refutes two implications: first, that the motion would apply to something that allows rest, and second, that if the quick moves a part, the slow must either match it (be equal), exceed it (be faster), or fall short (requiring division of the indivisible). The only remaining possibility is rests. He contrasts this with motion in place (al-haraka al-ayniyya), where the distance is a continuous extension admitting infinite divisions. An objection is raised: each finite unit might be infinitely divisible. The answer is that the transition to each unit is instantaneous, and the argument requires the overall extension to be continuous, not discrete. This refutes the mistaken notion that quantity, being intrinsically divisible, is even more fit for motion than distance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If motion is possible in distance, it is even more possible in quantity because quantity is intrinsically divisible.
Correction: The divisibility of distance is as a continuous extension; quantity in this context is a series of discrete states, so it does not support gradual motion.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say motion in place is different?
A) Because place is not a quantity.
B) Because the distance is a continuous single extension that admits infinite divisions.
C) Because motion in place is slower.
D) Because place is a quality.

Key Takeaway
Motion requires a continuous substrate that admits infinite potential division, which quantity and quality as discrete states lack.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe motion in the world—like a leaf floating from a tree—do you ever consider that it might not be composed of tiny instantaneous jumps? How does this lesson challenge your intuitive understanding of movement, and are you willing to accept a counterintuitive truth for the sake of sound reasoning about Allah's creation?
?
The objection in this lesson seems plausible at first glance. Where in your own faith journey have you accepted a seemingly reasonable argument without examining its deeper implications? Take one such belief you hold and commit to analyzing it with the same rigor shown here.
?
This lesson distinguishes between continuous and discrete motions. Does your concept of Allah's attribute of 'acting' align more with continuous creation or discrete interventions? How does this affect your daily sense of reliance on Him? What change in your heart is needed to embrace the full depth of kalam arguments?
